< Review>
Easy to notice from a moving vehicle. Large dining area with tables perfect for both small and large groups. They have one big screen tuned into the current soccer game. The minute you walk in, it smells like the delicious birria. They have a very simple menu with birria tacos ($2), tostadas, bowls of birria (full order is $10 and comes with tons of tortillas), canned/bottled sodas, and agua fresca. Food is served very quickly in plastic baskets, and is piping hot! That first bite reminded me of my abuelita's birria growing up. The only thing I wish this place had was air conditioning. The kitchen is so hot and steamy and opens up right into the dining area which makes it hot.< /Review>

< text>
So authentic you'll feel like you might actually be in TJ. Tried the birria tacos, birria tostada, and the orden grande birria bowl. If you aren't super hungry and just want to try birria I recommend the tacos, but if you want the full experience go for the bowl. You can get a half order too. My friend was a fan of the tostada, it has cheese melted and fried on it, but it was a little too crispy for me. I know, it's a tostada, that's the point - it's hard to explain, try one if you're curious and see if you like it. I think I'll try the quesadilla next time.<//text>

<review>Over the weekend I experienced what everyone's worst nightmare is.. a broken tooth. I was unaware of a cavity that had caused a lot of decay that resulted in a break. I knew that finding a dentist to treat me would be a difficult task because I am a cash patient (insurance doesn't kick in until March 1st). I was hesitant to even go because I knew I wouldn't be able to afford a crown etc with cash upfront, but convinced myself to go to one at least to see what it would take to fix my tooth.

I called Surf Smiles on 2/10/20 at about noon.. and they were able to fit me in same day! I mention that I was a cash patient and they quoted me a reasonable 89$ for a visit and x-rays. As I showed up to my appointment, I quickly noticed the well put together office. It's a beautiful spot. I was greeted by Dr. Hoeg at the front desk promptly and was asked to wait to be called. Not more than 10 minuted later, I was called to the back by Dr. Mark Warner who stated I would be seeing Dr. Hoeg for my appointment, but he was in a meeting so he would be starting my visit. (I thought that was very courteous because most of the time you're kept waiting when something like that occurs)

Dr. Mark Warner was very friendly and was quick to get my x-rays going. Dr. Hoeg came in shortly after and I was amazed by how nice he is!! Seriously just a genuinely nice individual. While I was getting my tooth looked at, Dr. Madeline Warner came in to introduce herself (seriously how nice is that?). I quickly realized that this practice is family run and they care about their patients as individuals. You're not just a number or price tag to this family! Dr. Hoeg continued to examine me and was very conservative in my treatment as he was trying to avoid a root canal (which I very much appreciate!!) I expressed to him that I am a cash pay patient and would be interested in a temporary solution to my tooth problem if need be until my insurance kicked in. I was blown away with his work ethic and compassion as he completely restored my tooth and was able to work with me on pricing. You literally can't even tell I had half of my tooth missing. (pictures listed as reference)

Not only am I (and my whole family) a patient for life, but I am actually excited to return and work on my other dental issues. I will continue to rave about this practice as long as they are in business! Thank you Surf Smiles, you have restored my smile (and faith in humanity).< /review></record></dataset><record>

< text>
The ambience and the concept are nicely executed here. The ingredients are seasonal, fresh and thoughtfully integrated into the cocktail and dinner menu. It was nice that they offered some nice mocktails to enjoy with our teenager. The rating is short of 5 stars because some of the plates and cocktails were really small proportions for high price (lots of ice in the cocktail tumbler and 5 smallish pieces of pork belly main). The service was energetic and enthusiastic and they did a great job with heating up the patio with lamps and a fire pit.< /text>

<rate>5</rate>< review>
I found The Lark on several lists so I felt compelled to try it. We reserved an early dinner and I must say I was impressed from beginning to end. The service was great, especially helping with entree sizes which can be varied at nicer restaurants. They started us with some complimentary seasoned popcorn which was an appreciated gesture, almost extinct in the food service world today. We followed it up with the burrata, which was served with wonderful Ojai pixies and olive tapenade. We finished out the meal with brussel sprouts and the pork belly. Every dish had a great blend of both familiar and unfamiliar flavors like habanero infused pineapple. Also, the mocktail list was appreciated!< /review>

< review>
They serve a tasty but not inexpensive meal in a casual and fun space, with friendly service, great drinks and a good wine list, but I agree with the more critical reviewers that the Chef overuses salt and spice. The dishes are also too complex for their own good. For example, the Valrhona chocolate cake featured a delicious cake, which was complimented by spicy cayenne pepper ice cream, coffee mousse, a very sweet brittle and raspberries--far too many flavors to work harmoniously together. In sum, not refined dining, but an enjoyable experience nonetheless.</review>

< Review>
I left The Lark feeling the restaurant was trying to hard and missing the mark. The atmosphere is very warm and inviting. Patio seating is intimate and quiet, inside is more loud and energized. Service is great, with welcoming staff, educated food runners and bar staff. Unique things like old factory windows, to heirloom silverware and decor transform the space into a unique eatery. We started with the cheese board, which had a average selection of cheeses. All was tasty and complete but nothing that blew me away. Our 2nd was a warm summer bean salad which was our favorite dish. The dish had nice flavors that touched many of the senses and was well balanced. We got the dungenous crab risotto for our entree and this had nice flavors but had way to much oil for my liking and enjoyment. The fresh squash and tomatoes In the dish were yummy. The biggest disappointment was the dessert and the Valharona chocolate cake. It did no justice to the famous maker and was bland and lacked flavor. The goat cheese cream was so salty that I believe that they stubbed their toe with the salt, perhaps confusing the salt and sugar. Wine list and beverage list was extensive and had many options. Plan on about $40pp or $70+pp with wine.</Review>

<username>Skyler Gamble< /username><Response>None< /Response></record></dataset><record>
<Date>1549504386002</Date>< text>
So this place made top 10 must eats in Santa Barbara. I believe that list should be revised. I'll start with the positives; knowledgeable and friendly staff, fresh local ingredients, generous appetizers, and good drinks.

Alas, the negatives outweigh positives. Salt and sweetness are being overused. It's the first time I had brussel sprouts smothered in sweet sauce which just totally killed the flavor for me. Leave them savory, sometimes Simplicity works much better. We could not finish the plate and had to rely on free popcorn to cleanse the palate; perhaps that's the reason they serve it. In addition, leaving them in the trunk for an hour gave birth to the most horrible smell I have yet experienced. I really thought I would need detailing afterwards and had flashback of that Seinfeld episode.

I did enjoy the salads and was curious enough to try the $50 prime rib dish. Although the dish was good and creative I can't say it was shareable unless you fill up an appetizers prior. It just left me feeling underwhelmed and prices are not worth the attempt at creativity and the quality of the meal.

The Lark may serve better as I happy hour with shareable appetizers among a large group. But this is not a dining experience.</text>

Dinner starts with an old milk bottle filled with tepid water. We had been wine tasting so we weren't ready for more drinking. I had to ask for a glass of ice because warm water doesn't work for me. Service was attentive. The ice arrived promptly. I sent the crispy Brussels sprouts back. Way too salty. The duck liver mousse arrived on blackened bread. Burnt black charcoal bread didn't pair well with the superb duck liver mousse .Sent that back. It came back on bread. The kitchen can't make decent toast? Whatever. Next came the Spanish grilled octopus with couscous served on a wood plank. Arrived cold. The chili rub really overwhelmed the flavor of the octopus. All I could taste was chili. The couscous with blood orange was decent but cold. Next came the grilled marinated hanger steak served with charred broccoli. I'm sorry, but 3 tiny pieces of meat for $16?

<review>Absolute disaster right from the start...Jazz our waitress took a long time to approach our table after we sat down. "Ill be with you in just a moment" would have been a wonderful gesture. Didn't happen. We ordered 2 cocktails - 2 appetizers and 2 entrees plus a bottle of sparkling water. I will list for you everything that went wrong:
1) We were brought tap water instead of sparkling water.
2) Our appetizers arrived before our cocktails offering us NO time to enjoy a drink before dinner.
3) It took 3 trips by Jazz to get my cocktail correct.
4) Before we were given the opportunity to finish our appetizes ..our entrees arrived.
5) We were never offered another cocktail..or another bottle of water.
6) When our appetizer plates were removed Jazz took our fork and knife...we now had our entrees with no utensils to eat our food. As our food got cold my husband had to get up and find a table to retrieve utensils.
7) I asked for lemon for my fish which did not arrive till our meal was over.
8) My trout just didn't taste that good! That was what the lemon was for!

The only thing we enjoyed were the brussel sprouts and the ice cubes were cold enough to cool our water!

Stop trying to be hip ... Stop trying to be cool and trendy and focus on teaching your staff the basics of customer service.

My nephew who lives here said The Lark is over priced ...Over rated and as a local would NEVER eat here. We should have listened to him.

Do not eat here ...You'll be very disappointed...

As a consolation our cocktails were on the house.

<date>1523735299420<//date><Rate>2<//Rate><Review>After all the hype and enthusiastic recommendations online for this restaurant I was disappointed by it's lack of originality, over packed environment, unfriendly service and bad music bad music..

The food was less than inspiring. Served family style.

We skipped the brussel sprouts as even though it's the main attraction (what mainstream hipster restaurant hasn't got brussel sprouts as their main attraction since 2011??!). We shared the spring veggies, which were overloaded with chickpeas and doused in the "flavor of the moment" cumin, which overpowered what could have been a nice fresh dish. The hamachi was very good, a really nice combination of flavors, that were thoughtfully put together, although the melon wasnt fully ripe, but still the best part of our dish. Finally the duck wings were crispy and spicy but overall lacking in meat and in the end we both gave up as it wasn't worth the effort.

The drinks were good and we loved the free popcorn it was salt and vinegar flavor a nice snack while we waited on our dishes. After asking for a little more though our server never returned üòÖ.

Overall the decor and ambiance echos any hipster feel that has been going on for years in Portland, SF, LA and Austin, it's a shame the restaurant doesn't embrace a more unique Santa Barbara feel in it's design and menu.<//Review><Pics>None</Pics>< resp>

< Text>
Overall disappointing experience, since we had traveled from San Diego and made a weekend of it just to eat at The Lark.  Our server was new and unfamiliar with the wines and menu.  She clowned a bit to cover her lack of experience, which took away from our dinner together (my husband and I.)  So it all became about her.  The food was merely ok --   certainly not San Francisco calibre.  It's been a month since we ate there and I can't tell you what we had, except for a tough, uninteresting steak and lackluster pimento cheese with a few measly croutons.  The tables for two are insultingly small, especially for a restaurant that only serves shared plates.  The one standout was our Brewer-Clifton Pinot.  The atmosphere feels like a chain restaurant, which is sad since the design is so lovely.  I will say that we like The Lucky Penny a lot and also the wine shop and wine bar behind The Lark.  For them I'll give two more stars than The Lark deserves.<//Text>

< Review>
As part of our road trip across california my fiance and I stopped off here for dinner this evening. We were glad to have made a reservation as it was very busy. We bought a bottle of wine to sip on whilst we waited for our  table to free up (cheapest sauvingnon blanc..and it was delicious) . The menu had so many delicious options.. we were spoilt for choice. But we went for the Brussels spouts  (delicious signature starter), steak tartar  (again yummy), the burrata  (peaches cheese and praline...absolutely divine), the pork belly (3 ways and smoky crispy goodness with a peach and nut brittle) and the lamb ribs (falling off the bone). Would definitely recommend to anyone! Wish we could go again. Rich and lucy from England<//Review>

<user>102703854051050458502<//user>< pics>
None</pics>
< Date>
1376613278379<//Date>
< Text>
This restaurant is a little unreal, and I love it. First some background - The Lark took over the old Bay Cafe space in the Funk Zone. The Funk Zone has been going through it's "renaissance" for a number of years but I feel only within the last one year has it really come together. The Funk Zone is like the Brooklyn of Santa Barbara. It's a little grungy and kitchy but things are really looking good there.

I went the week after it opened and it was packed with people. Their parking lot was full and they were offering valet parking, which is a good thing since there's nowhere to park in that neighborhood. We sat outside and while it was chilly, we were under some decent heatlamps. There are also fire pits and blue blankets you can use if you are cold.

Everything is family style and meant to be shared. Our waitress was very knowledgeable but a little pushy on the upsell. Luckily, we resisted her charms and didn't order one of the large entrees. We still had plenty of food though. Alot of the dishes came out in the wrong order and they gave our scallop dish to another table altogether, resulting in at least a 20 minute delay. There was no offer of comping a drink or dessert (easy things to do).

The mixed drinks were good (but not great). The food was excellent and the desserts really were some of the best in SB; really inventive and interesting with multiple layers or flavor and textures.

You should definitely go check it out if you are into a leisurely meal. Make sure you account for parking.</Text>
